Summary

What happens when Rio Vidal is down on her luck and cleaning shit out of cages to earn money to pay for her degree?

She gets desperate.

What happens when she gets desperate?

She agrees to a tentative arrangement with a hot forty-something woman she met at a bar and fucked while hammered to join together and do something a little more... lucrative.

With a strangers-with-benefits title beneath their belts, what could it hurt to film their escapades and make some money while doing it?

Alas, a double edged sword.

Rio could show up and take care of her friend, no matter how much Agatha tried to fight her, or she could show up to find out Agatha was (for whatever reason) lying to her. Both scenarios had very high probabilities of her being turned away.

While it might have been a foregone conclusion that Agatha was trying to keep her away, Rio couldn’t help herself. She, in fact, couldn’t help herself so much that she barely heard a single word of her afternoon lecture, far too preoccupied by thoughts of Agatha.

She knew it was in her best interest to downplay whatever weird connection was between them; they were just friends on a surface level, their conversations were never actually deep, and when it came down to it, Rio was certain Agatha would call someone else in a crisis. After all, they’d only known each other a few months.

It didn’t matter that it felt like they’d been acquainted their whole lives.

That wasn’t important.

That couldn’t be important.

Yet it didn’t stop her from wanting to care. Someone that mattered to her was sick and if she could do anything about it, it was damn sure going to try.

After a class where she learned absolutely nothing, Rio packed her things and headed to a nearby diner on campus. Five minutes later, she walked out with a small bag and a container of chicken noodle soup tucked inside.

Whatever the risk of showing up, Rio would mitigate the cost. At the very least, she just had to know for herself that Agatha was okay.

She climbed out of the car, bag in hand and her messenger bag over her shoulder and made her way up Agatha’s front steps. When she reached the top, she knew she had a decision to make.

So, she tapped twice on the door with her knuckles first.

No answer.

Two more taps.

Still no answer.

So she tried the handle next.

Surprisingly, it gave and turned to the right, allowing her entry.

She scanned the living room, half expecting Agatha to be curled up on the couch with a box of tissues, but was met with an empty and unoccupied room. As she turned to shut the door, a surprised sound came from behind her.

“Oh. “

When she spun in place, the last thing Rio expected was to see Agatha fully dressed in a pair of dark jeans and a violet sweater, hair done, and face made up.

Her stomach sank instantly.

“You don't look very sick, “ Rio stated with a neutral tone from her place by the door as Agatha reached the bottom of the stairs, clearly caught off guard.

“Who just walks into someone’s house?” Agatha questioned coolly, gliding toward the kitchen.

Rio bristled immediately, her face pinching in annoyance.

“Cut the shit, Agatha,” Rio clipped, following her to set the soup down on the small table. “What's going on? Why are you bailing and lying about it?” She hesitated on the far side of the kitchen, her arms folded protectively over her torso.

Rio never once felt the need to keep Agatha out in such a way before, but she did not take kindly to being lied to.

It didn't matter.

Agatha couldn't see it anyway. She was too busy pouring herself – and only herself – a drink.

The longer she took to answer, the more Rio could feel that annoyance ebbing, replaced by something stronger.

Anger.

Fear.

Confusion.

Worry.

Why was Agatha shutting her out? Moreover, why was Agatha straight up trying to ignore her when she was right there?

“I have things I need to do,” she finally replied, raising her glass a second later to take a long draw from it.

“And you couldn't just tell me that?” Rio snapped. She shifted her weight from one foot to the other, practically staring a hole in Agatha's back the entire time. “I don't believe you. “

Maybe it was rude, maybe it was mean. Rio didn't care. What Agatha was doing right then felt mean. She was lying, she was shutting down, and all Rio wanted to do was help.

“It doesn't matter, Rio.” That was sharp. It was cold. It was so… Un-Agatha that it was jarring.

“It does ma–”

“I just needed a break!” she shouted, her hands flying out as she spun in a dramatic fashion. There was a wild look in her eyes Rio did not understand and honestly, it worried her.

What the actual fuck was going on?

How was this happening?

“A break?” Rio scoffed, rolling her eyes as her arms tightened around her ribs. “A break right before we’re supposed to fulfill our end of a creator/consumer bargain?”

“Oh fuck you,” Agatha sneered. “It’s not about the sex and you know it.”

Honestly, the ‘fuck you’ stung something awful, but Rio instead needed to focus on the latter half of Agatha’s statement.

Because Rio did know it. Agatha liked to take as much as she liked to give; it was a known fact between them.

So what actually had her that upset?

“So then tell me what it is about! We've been friends for months at this point, Agatha. Why the fuck are you suddenly lying to me?”

It was a fair question, she thought.

Agatha did not seem to agree.

“I don't owe you anything.”

Was she fucking serious? They set up this entire business arrangement at her behest and now she didn't even owe Rio so much as the truth?

What the fuck was going on with her?

Rio’s gaze narrowed, sharp and cutting as it swept over the woman before her.

“Is that how this goes? You wrangle me in just to fulfill some ego trip for you and when you're bored, you just give me the boot?” She was being harsh, and she could tell as much by the way Agatha's angry mask was starting to slip. “That's all it is, right? Fucking ego? Because it sure as fuck isn't about money for you, is it?!”

Agatha’s scowl was gone, but her cheeks and forehead were still a deep, deep crimson.

“It doesn't matter.”

It was the second time she said it and somehow, it pissed Rio off more than the first.

“You keep fucking saying that like it's an answer. It's not an answer, Agatha! What was in it for you?!”

Rio didn't actually expect an answer. In fact, she was quite certain they were well past the point of having a productive conversation. So when Agatha snapped back with an answer almost immediately, Rio was rather stunned.

“I just needed a fucking friend! Accountability!” Before she even finished speaking, her hand flew downward and the sound of shattering glass almost overtook her last word.

Fuck.

How did they get to that point?

But accountability?

What did that even mean?

She should have deescalated, she knew she should have, but something in Rio was already too fired up to let it go.

“I don't even know what that means! Accountability for what?!”

That time, when Rio looked up from the shattered glass and whiskey on the floor, she did not see an angry or enraged Agatha.

She saw an upset Agatha instead. A tired Agatha.

An Agatha who, unbeknownst to her, was tired of running.

“It genuinely doesn't matter, Rio. Please leave.”

Agatha was getting really good at saying words that felt like physical blows, especially with that tone of voice.

How did any of this happen?

“Can you…” Rio started, stepping forward with the intent of helping Agatha clean up. “Can you just talk to me?”

When Agatha issued her command again, the frantic and elevated tone she used before returned and her hands flew up to ward Rio off, as if the gesture alone would push her away.

“Get out of my house!”

Rio didn't want to. She didn't want to listen and take the coward’s way out. She didn’t want to turn her back on someone she cared about when it was clear they were going through something.

“Please, Agatha…”

“I’m not going to tell you again.”

That was dangerous. It was a threat.

“Okay,” Rio offered in surrender, holding her hands up as she took a step back.

She hated it.

She fucking hated it.

She just wanted to know what was wrong.

She just wanted to talk.

But Agatha did not, and it was her house.

“Have a good night, Agatha.”

When Rio shut the door behind her, she couldn’t help but wonder if it was the last time she would get to do so. It was dramatic, maybe, and maybe this was something they could talk about and work through, but it felt pretty final.

Maybe it was true she’d never seen Agatha angry before, and was living with rose colored glasses on because of it, but her anger felt so unwarranted and exaggerated.

Even on the thirty minute walk home, Rio failed to come up with any logical rationale that would or could possibly explain what happened. She had the simple facts, sure, but they made no sense without some kind of explanation.

An explanation she might never get.

Of course, there was no way she was going to simply lie down and give up, but Rio knew as she showered and settled into bed, they both needed some time. Surely it was not Agatha’s intention to completely dissolve their friendship or their working relationship, but she sure as shit needed to work through whatever the fuck was going on in that head of hers.

Whatever it was, it would work itself out.

It had to.

It was Rio’s second to last thought before she fell asleep.

Her very last thought was that she could try again tomorrow.

 

Chapter 21: The Text.

Chapter Notes

Hiiii again! Thanks as always for every comment, every kudos, every minute you spend reading this!!!! It means so much, seriously. I may have to say I have the majority of this story already written out which is why I've been doing daily drops, but I will try to show restraint!!! Maybe!!! Probably not!!!

When Rio woke up the next morning, everything felt wrong.

She was in her own bed on a Saturday morning and absolutely no plans to fill her weekend with the usual company.

Agatha’s company.

Because, upon some early morning reflection, Rio realized she might have made a misstep or two.

She panicked and as a result, she overreacted.

Agatha was right:

Who the fuck just walked into someone’s house? Even more, who walked into someone’s house just to berate and accost them for a personal choice they made? Agatha was well within her rights to turn Rio away, to demand that she leave.

Whether she lied or not, Agatha’s need for space had been apparent and Rio chose to ignore it. She knew she was trying to be a good and caring friend, but she crossed too many lines in the process and if Agatha’s response to that was to shut her out?

She kind of deserved it.

Honestly, maybe if she’d been honest with Agatha before that point, she could have explained herself better, but it didn’t really matter, not actually. Because no matter how afraid she was of being left behind, it was no excuse for exhibiting a flagrant disregard for Agatha’s boundaries.

If she was real with herself, she was worried. The truth was, their friendship was still rather new and while it was months long at that point, she was afraid she hadn’t given Agatha enough to think she was worth forgiving. It wasn’t like she committed the ultimate indiscretion, but she had been disrespectful. There was no denying that.

But it was only because Rio knew the truth, her truth.

She couldn’t lose Agatha.

It wasn’t about the sex, or the porn, or the money. All three of those things were nice, sure, but they weren’t what mattered most.

No, that was Agatha herself.

It was her scrunched nose when Rio made a bad joke. It was her laughter when Rio made a good joke. It was the way she stuck her tongue out or pouted when she was being a brat. It was the strength of her embraces and the intensity of her kisses. It was those sleepy smiles first thing in the morning and the kisses to her hairline at night.

Rio had long since admitted to herself that her attraction to Agatha ran far deeper than just the physical and even seeped further down than even sexual.

Maybe if she could have been a grown ass woman instead of a little bitch and just told Agatha the truth, she wouldn’t have been alone.

And she had an entire fucking day to be alone.

It wasn’t the worst thing in the world (yes it was) and gave her time to tend to her own dwelling, picking up around her apartment and even deciding to deep clean and rearrange her furniture.

After what felt like half the day, Rio flipped her phone over to check the time and frowned deeply, severely disappointed by what she saw.

It was barely two in the afternoon.

And she did not have a single text message.

Because why in her right mind would Agatha even consider texting her?

Could that really just be… it?

Could they really just end, just like that?

The thought alone made Rio want to text her, to say she was sorry or she hoped they could talk soon, but she buried the urge. The last thing she needed to do was apply any more pressure and end up wrecking her chances for good.

So what the fuck did she do for the rest of the day?

After a shower and a later lunch, she turned on the TV in the front room and laid herself across the couch, wasting twenty minutes alone trying to find something to watch. After settling on some Scottish procedural drama, she grabbed the blanket off the back of the couch and got comfortable.

Too comfortable.

When she woke up, it was half past six.

Fuck. Oops.

When she grabbed her phone, something in her chest ached to see no new messages.

It sucked.

It was the consequences of her own fucking actions and it sucked.

With a sigh, Rio quickly ran a mental lap of all the things she could possibly do to keep herself busy, finally landing at the last –and probably worst – one.

She would go to the bar.

Terrible idea, especially if Agatha had the same one, but it sure beat the hell out of laying around in her own misery. At least the bar had strong alcohol and a Jen who would probably hassle the hell out of her if she noticed the state Rio was in.

Because Jen?

She didn’t do nice.

She did “bully you to the point of realizing life could be much, much worse.”

It was better than Rio bullying herself, honestly. While she could be a nuisance to others, she was often her own worst enemy and beating herself down was never going to end well.

Jen doing it for her?

That was different. It was motivation.

With another defeated sigh, Rio forced herself up and then got to her feet, lazily slinking to her bedroom to get dressed.

She could have put on something showy or flashy, something that would undeniably pull the attention of other occupants, but…

She didn’t really want to.

Yeah, sure, maybe she wanted to go to the bar to drink and forget about whatever Agatha might possibly be doing without her around, but she didn’t want to act like Agatha didn’t matter at all by going home with someone else. She was upset and maybe a little nervous, but she wasn’t a fucking asshole.

So, per her typical hobo-chic style, she climbed into a pair of sweatpants, pulled a thin hoodie over her head and tied her hair in a messy knot on top of her head, not a shit given about what she looked like.

If Agatha wasn’t the one looking, she didn’t really care.

After grabbing her keys and wallet, she made her way out and meandered down the block to the bar, enjoying the cool evening air all the while. When she reached the front door, she hesitated, bracing herself for what she was going to walk into.

She was so right to do it too, mostly because when she pulled it open and stepped inside, the most obnoxiously shrill scream hit her ears.

“Oh my GOD!” Jen shrieked from behind the bar, crystal clear for the six other occupants to hear. “We can call off the search party! Lilia! Get the Coast Guard on the phone! Tell them she’s finally come home!”

The older woman down the bar top simply rolled her eyes and waved a hand at her empty wine glass, very obviously demanding a refill.

“I fucking hate you, you certified drama queen,” Rio grumbled as she climbed onto a stool, leaning on her forearms over the bar as Jen appeared in front of her with a wickedly devious grin.

“Sooooo, whatcha been up to, Vidal? It’s been fucking months. Did she finally dump your ass?”

Fucking ow.

That wasn’t nice.

But it should have been expected.

It was Jennifer Fucking Kale and her very, very limited tact.

“What makes you think I didn’t dump her first?”

She knew she shouldn’t have fucking said anything, but she really knew she shouldn’t have said anything when Jen practically grew fangs.

“Because it’s you we’re talking about. You’d sooner let her step on you in stilettos and put cigarettes out on your skin than dump her first.”

Jesus fucking Christ.

Who the fuck pissed in her Wheaties that morning?

“You’re being especially awful before I even order a drink,” Rio pointed out, but Jen ignored her and turned around, reaching up for the bottle of WhistlePig that sat on the top shelf. Without a word, she filled it and slid it across the bar, causing it to bump against Rio’s arm, sloshing a bit over it.

“That one’s on the house because you look like shit. You’re drinking Jack the rest of the night.”

Rio wanted to argue just to spite the other woman and insist she could drink top shelf liquor all she wanted, but she knew it was stupid. She might have had thousands of dollars within Agatha’s control, but she barely had enough on her to get sufficiently drunk.

So she threw the shot back, grateful. She was even more grateful when a shot of Jack miraculously appeared in front of her, too.

Above it was an open palm, clearly wanting something in return.

Right.

Money.

The thing she shouldn’t be spending.

But it was better than wallowing around in her own home, sad and pathetic.

Being pathetic was more fun with an audience, right?

With a sigh, Rio pulled her card out of her wallet and slapped it into Jen’s awaiting hand, rolling her eyes as the other woman squeaked delightedly and turned away to stow the card for safe keeping.

“Anything exciting happen around here lately?” Rio asked just before tossing her shot back.

“She had to throw two kids out the other night. It was pretty funny,” Lilia, the older woman a few seats down offered with a dry laugh.

“It was not funny! That one little shit just kept doing laps around the fucking bar,” she snapped, leveling the other woman with a pointed glare.

Lilia snorted into her wine.

Clearly she did not agree.

“What about you? Commit any crimes in your months-long absence?”

That was stupid. Jen knew she wasn’t the crime-doing type, but it was obvious she was trying to keep the mood light.

“Depends,” Rio answered, sliding the glass over to ask for another shot. As Jen complied and refilled the glass, she raised a brow to prompt her to keep talking. “Just how stupid can one person be until it’s considered a crime?”

While Jen never passed up an opportunity to give Rio hell, she seemed to especially adore those moments – however few and far between they were – where Rio took on the task before she could. Her laughter was undeniable proof.

“That depends. Did you drop out?”

That was actually the most offensive thing Jen probably could have said.

But in her defense, it did play into the conversation.

“No,” Rio returned, trying not to snap. “Not yet anyway. But… I don’t want to talk about it tonight.”

A low whistle sounded from between Jen’s teeth before she sucked on them and readied her next assault.

“Tou-chee, jeez,” she grumbled, wiping down a portion of the bar to Rio’s left.

“Oh, fuck off and pour me another shot,” Rio said gruffly before pounding back the one in front of her.

Thirty minutes and two shots later, Rio was drunk.

She wasn’t ‘go home with a random stranger and spend the next three months fucking them relentlessly under the guise of a good business model’ drunk, but she was pretty toasted.

So when she pulled out her phone, the smallest voice in the back of her head tried to tell her to put it back.

Rio In Charge did not listen to that voice even a little.

Instead, she saw the empty screen and decided to do something about it.

She was going to text Agatha.

Yeah!

But she had to be smart about it.

Boo!

At least she wasn’t so drunk that she lost every bit of sense she possessed. In a weekend filled with losses, that was actually a win.

Rio leaned back on the stool, her focus trained on the phone in her hands. She could do it. She had to do it.

The silence was fucking killing her.

She couldn’t take it anymore.

“Hi, Agatha. Its me, Rio. I just wanted to tell you im sorry. I overstepped like bad and i Really shouldn’t have. Because you matter to me and your feelings do. And I am really sorry. I know I should have just waited til you were ready to see me again I guess I just got nervous that you might not want to. See me again i mean. And then maybe because i was An Asshole and came in uninvited now you might really not want to see me again. And really thats actually pretty fair. Cuz I was an asshole. And I would deserve it. But I hope maybe we can talk soon and I can tell you how sorry I am in person. I still don’t know what you meant by accountability but I AM your friend. Well i want to be if we can still be friends. Im sorry Agatha. I hope you have a good night.”

Too drunk to give it a second thought, she pressed the send button and locked her phone. When she lifted her head to ask Jen for a glass of water, she was already marching her way down with one in hand.

“Figured you’d want one before you head home,” she jabbed lightly, causing Rio to pout.

“Is that you kicking me out?”

“No, it’s me knowing that look on your face. Any more and we both know you’ll regret it. You can stay as long as you like, but I’ll close your tab.”

Jen was right. She didn’t need to hammer herself into a blackout state and end up pantless, hung over someone’s backyard fence.

“I hate that you’re a bartender who gives more of a shit about your patrons’ wellbeing than money. You fucking enigma.”

Jen barked a laugh, sliding the receipt over for Rio to sign, which she did only after leaving a $10 tip. She would probably regret it in the morning, but Jen deserved it.

“You can’t come back and spend money if you convince me to give you alcohol poisoning and you die.”

That time, it was Rio’s turn to laugh.

“You have a fair point.”

“Drink up, Vidal.”

Halfway through her glass of water, a miracle happened.

Her phone buzzed on the bar.

🦊

1 New Message

Holy shit.

With unsteady and shaking fingers, Rio opened the message.

“I can tell you’re drunk, but thank you for the apology. Have a good night, Rio.”

That was it?

That was all she –

Actually.

With a deep and slow breath, Rio reframed her thinking.

Agatha said it best.

Technically, she didn’t owe Rio a thing.

Any response was a gift and she realized she should take it as such. Instead of rushing to reply, she finished her water, thanked Jen for the kind service and headed out the door and up the street, finding herself at home ten minutes later.

When she crawled into bed, she pulled her phone out one last time and finally typed her response.

“Goodnight, Agatha. I promise to do better.”

When the phone locked and hit the pillow next to her head, it took about thirty seconds for her to fall asleep.

 

Chapter 22: The Amends.

Chapter Notes

Hiii!!! Will thank you all til the end of time!!! You're all amazing and adored by me with your kind words and silly comments and support!!! AHHHH!!!! But uhm. Yeah.... Okay. Anyway... Have fun.........

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Unfortunately for Rio, Sunday morning was much of the same, only with a minor headache and an upset stomach thrown in for added flair.

When she woke up, it was to an empty lock screen and not a sign of Agatha to be seen.

Oh god.

What did that text even say?

Rio remembered texting her, of course, but she could not remember exactly what was said in the process. When she pulled up the conversation and briefly skimmed over the wall of text she’d composed the night before, she felt like she was going to be sick. It wasn’t bad, per say, and it was far from terrible, but fuck if it wasn’t embarrassing as hell.

Especially when Agatha called her out for being drunk.

While yes, she was an adult and was capable of doing whatever adult activity she wanted to do, she was not above feeling like a scolded child when someone she cared about pointed out her bad behavior.

Getting drunk was fine. Texting Agatha in the midst of it was where she might have fucked up.

Then again, it wasn’t like Agatha’s response was cruel or mean. Maybe a little annoyed, but she did thank Rio for the apology, no matter how choppy and poorly worded it was. Maybe Agatha saw her intent over her delivery and that was why she chose to show gratitude instead of getting upset. Even if she would have been angry… Well, Rio felt like she deserved it.

However.

The original question still hadn’t been answered.

Why did Agatha bail and lie about it?

There was clearly something Rio was missing, some piece of Agatha she couldn’t see to help her figure out what was going on, but she knew something was wrong. While they’d been friends for a solid three – almost four – months, it honestly felt like so much longer. It felt like they’d been friends for years and yet, they still didn’t know so much about each other, about what made them who they were.

What if they would have just had those conversations? What if Rio would have gotten the will to be honest about why she was in college in her mid-thirties and why she was working so hard to get her damn degree.

Would Agatha have talked back?

Would she have admitted all the things that turned her into a charismatic recluse who (more often than not) scared the townspeople? Would she have told Rio why she was sitting on a fortune and living an otherwise mundane life?

Did it matter now?

She was still half-convinced Agatha might never speak to her again.

That made for a fun Sunday.

At least for a couple of hours, Rio managed to distract herself by going to the store to stock up for the week on groceries. As it stood, she was quite certain she would be spending the following week alone and purchased a six pack of beer in anticipation.

Jen might bitch again, but whiskey was fucking expensive.

She toiled away her day by touching up a few spots she’d missed the day before on her cleaning spree and tried to distract herself with television first to no avail, and then ended up scouring the app store for some mindless game to play. That didn’t work either.

By the time the sun began to drop in the sky, she knew she should probably feed herself. It was a quick dinner of ramen with a chicken breast and some extra chili oil, but it fed the machine and caused her stomach to stop all the noise it was making.

Less than an hour after sundown, Rio couldn’t take it anymore.

All she did as she cleaned and watched TV and played on her stupid phone was think about Agatha, about how she was still quiet and probably upset. She knew they needed to have a conversation, they both did. So why was she prolonging it?

Rio hated it.

Chewing on her lip, she picked up her phone and slowly typed a message.

“Can I come over?”

She knew the likely answer would be no, but it didn’t hurt to ask at the very least. She sent the message and laid her phone on the back of the couch, wandering down the hallway to the bathroom. Mid-pee, she heard her phone go off.

That was fast.

Could be good.

Could be bad.

Either way, she needed to know.

After washing her hands, she scrambled out and grabbed up her phone, opening Agatha’s message instantly.

🦊

“You can do anything you want. There is no one to stop you. But it doesn’t mean I have to let you in.”

That was actually a fair response, even if it was kind of annoying. Rio sighed, staring down at her phone with a deep crease in her brow. It wasn’t exactly an invitation, but it wasn’t a flat out ‘no’ either. That was for a reason. Because Agatha was intentional, always.

“Okay. I’m coming over.”

It was a quick response and Rio was off, pulling on a sweatshirt and pair of pants over her shorts before her feet slipped into shoes and she was out the door, ordering a ride.

When she arrived at Agatha’s and slowly made her way up the front walk, she realized she didn’t have a plan. What was she supposed to do if Agatha really wasn’t going to let her in, like she said? It might have seemed like a good idea to jump at what little she was given, but she hadn’t taken the time to actually parse it out and figure out the best way to tackle it.

The only place she could start was to knock on the door, so she did.

“I meant what I said.”

It was close, way too close, like Agatha was already at the door.

“That you’re not going to let me in?” Rio asked back softly, pressing her forehead to the small crack where the frame and the door met.

“Yes.”

Well, shit. She should have expected it; rarely did Agatha say things she didn’t mean, but maybe she’d been a little disillusioned in her blind hope to think once she got there, Agatha might change her mind.

“Okay,” Rio said, exhaling a soft sigh. “Is it okay with you if I sit down? You can turn the porch light out so no one sees me.”

Maybe it was stupid to insist she was going to stay, but at least that time she had the decency to ask.

“Yes.”

And just like that, the light above her head went out. She peeled her head back from the cold wood of the door and heaved another quiet sigh, staring at it for a moment before she lowered herself to the ground and pressed her back to it. Not a moment later, she felt the tiniest shift in the door as Agatha sat down on the other side and leaned against it.

The silence for Rio was only broken by the soft sound of crickets chirping away, singing their song to the night. She heard nothing on the other side of the door, but the way it jostled slightly every so often reminded Rio that Agatha was still there.

It had to have been at least ten minutes by the time Rio decided she could no longer take the silence.

“I want to tell you something,” she began, only loud enough to be heard through the door. She pulled her knees up to her chest and tucked her arms in, picking at her cuticles in nothing more than a nervous habit.

“When I was eighteen, my younger brother was in a pretty bad car accident. It… It paralyzed him from the neck down and he was in a coma for two months. When he came out of it… He needed a lot of attention.” She fell quiet and took in a deep breath, trying to level herself. “That fell to me. I didn’t have a steady job or a household to take care of. All I was going to do was go to college, but Mateo needed me. So I was there.”

There was the softest tremble to her voice, one she tried hard to fight.

“When I was twenty, he finally passed and I know it was the happiest day for him. He was so fucking miserable, so hopeless. And I never blamed him. Two years later… My dad had a stroke. It happened at work and led to an accident, so it wasn’t just the typical, run-of-the-mill tragic life-altering circumstance. It got a lot worse.”

Part of Rio wanted to stop, to get up off that front porch and just walk away, but she knew she owed it to Agatha to be honest.

“Three years later, he died, too. And even with me still around, and twenty-five, it wasn’t enough for my mom. The doctors said her heart gave out, but I think she just died of loneliness. Her son, her husband were both gone and I…”

Rio exhaled a devastated chuckle, hanging her head.

“I wasn’t good enough for her to keep going. So… I took time to mourn and to grieve. I buried the three people I loved most in a six year span. And it fucking sucked. And that… That’s why I’m in my thirties trying to finish my last fucking year of my masters. Because I… I still want to be someone.”
